‚ÄúManifest Destiny: A Legacy of Roman Colonialism and Its Modern Implications in American Politics and Nativ Minority Struggles‚Äù

Introduction

The United States‚Äô history is fraught with instances of violence and systemic displacement of Indigenous peoples. Central to this process was Manifest Destiny, a 19th-century ideology that promoted the expansion of the U.S. from the Atlantic to the Pacific Oceans (Smith, 2018). The belief that Americans were divinely ordained to settle the continent fueled the dispossession of Native lands. However, this wasn‚Äôt solely a secular mission‚Äîit was deeply intertwined with religious institutions, particularly the Catholic Church. Through its influence over Indigenous boarding schools, the Church was complicit in widespread cultural destruction and abuse (Jackson, 2021). Moreover, Roman autocracy‚Äôs co-optation of Christianity for political ends has left a legacy of religious manipulation that continues to affect marginalized groups today (Miller, 2022).

The Doctrine of Manifest Destiny and its Impact

Manifest Destiny was an expansionist political doctrine and a divine mandate. Many European Americans justified their right to expand and conquer Indigenous lands based on the belief that it was their God-given duty (Brown, 2019). This allowed settlers to engage in violent and oppressive actions with moral impunity, as the displacement of Native tribes was framed as part of a broader civilizing mission. Treaties such as the Fort Laramie Treaty of 1868, which was supposed to protect Indigenous lands, were ignored as soon as economic interests, such as the discovery of gold in the Black Hills, arose (U.S. Department of the Interior, 2021). The doctrine also had deep connections to the Catholic Church, whose involvement in colonization extended through missionary work and the establishment of boarding schools. By merging religion with expansionism, the U.S. government and Church leaders justified the subjugation of Indigenous peoples (Miller, 2022). Manifest Destiny provided the ideological framework for what would become one of the most destructive campaigns against Native populations in U.S. history.

Catholic Boarding Schools and Cultural Genocide

Perhaps one of the darkest chapters in U.S. history was the establishment of Catholic-run boarding schools, where Indigenous children were forcibly removed from their homes and placed under the control of clergy. These institutions were designed to assimilate Native children into European American culture by erasing their identities, languages, and traditions (Jackson, 2021). Tragically, many children suffered from physical and sexual abuse at the hands of priests, a crime that has been covered up for decades (Smith, 2021). Recent discoveries of mass graves near former boarding schools in Canada and the U.S. have shed light on the extent of the abuse (Smith, 2021). The Catholic Church‚Äôs role in this cultural genocide is undeniable, as these schools were often funded and operated under the guise of religious charity. This systemic abuse left lasting scars on Indigenous communities, contributing to generational trauma that persists today (Jackson, 2021).

The Black Hills Lawsuit and Modern Indigenous Resistance

The legal fight for the Black Hills represents a pivotal moment in the ongoing struggle of Indigenous peoples for justice. After gold was discovered in the Black Hills‚Äîland sacred to the Sioux‚Äîthe U.S. government seized the territory in direct violation of the Fort Laramie Treaty (U.S. Department of the Interior, 2021). Decades later, in 1980, the Supreme Court ruled that the U.S. had stolen the Black Hills and ordered financial compensation. However, the Sioux rejected the monetary award, insisting their sacred land be returned (White & Green, 2020). This legal victory, while significant, underscores the limitations of colonial law. For the Sioux, the land itself is irreplaceable, and the U.S. government‚Äôs refusal to return it demonstrates the continued marginalization of Indigenous sovereignty (Smith, 2018). Modern movements like ‚ÄúLand Back‚Äù are part of a broader push for the restitution of Indigenous lands and the decolonization of U.S. policies (Brown, 2019).

Roman Autocracy and the Manipulation of Catholic Doctrine

The connection between Roman autocracy and Catholicism dates back to the Roman Empire when political leaders saw the Church as a means of controlling the masses (Miller, 2022). Roman emperors adopted Christianity as the state religion, using its teachings to justify their power and control over the population. This manipulation of religion has continued throughout history, with the Catholic Church often allying itself with political powers to maintain influence. In the U.S., this legacy of religious manipulation is evident in the role the Catholic Church played in colonizing Indigenous lands and oppressing marginalized communities (Jackson, 2021). The Church‚Äôs involvement in Manifest Destiny and the boarding school system shows how religion has been used to justify expansion and cultural destruction under the guise of moral superiority (Miller, 2022).

The Second Gilded Age and Modern Parallels

Today, the U.S. is in what many scholars call the Second Gilded Age‚Äîa period characterized by extreme wealth inequality and corporate influence over politics (White & Green, 2020). Much like during the first Gilded Age, when Manifest Destiny was in full swing, modern political elites used propaganda and religious rhetoric to maintain control. The influence of the Catholic Church and other religious institutions can still be seen in political movements that promote nationalism and exclusionary policies. This period also marks a resurgence in Indigenous activism, as movements like the Fight for the Black Hills and Land Back seek to reclaim stolen lands and restore sovereignty to Native nations (Smith, 2018). Indigenous peoples are at the forefront of resistance to modern forms of colonialism, challenging the structures that have oppressed them for centuries (Brown, 2019).



Conclusion

Manifest Destiny, the Catholic Church‚Äôs involvement in boarding schools, and the legal fight for the Black Hills all demonstrate the ongoing impact of colonialism on Indigenous communities. By merging political power with religious authority, the U.S. government and the Catholic Church justified the violent expansion and displacement of Native peoples. Today, Indigenous communities continue to resist these structures, asserting their rights to land and sovereignty in the face of ongoing marginalization. As the Second Gilded Age unfolds, it is crucial to recognize the parallels between past and present and to support efforts for decolonization and justice.

Cenk,

I have to disagree with you here.

Regarding NATO promising Russia that it will not expand anymore: that was never a binding agreement. But let's assume it was, Russia asked Ukraine to return their nuclear weapons for security in 1991. Yet, Russia invaded Ukraine.

Long-range weapons into Russian territory would help Ukraine stop the Russian advances and better negotiate a cease-fire. Most left-wing Europeans have been asking that for a while. 

Recently, Russia changed its nuclear doctrine. In my opinion, it's a way to scare the West into not providing any more weapons to Ukraine. But here's the thing, Russia was the one escalating and threatening the world with nuclear weapons. 

Here's a scenario: let's say Russia did use nuclear weapons (battlefield or city-killer) on Ukraine. Do you think the West would say "We'll stop providing weapons"? Absolutely not, they will retaliate and destroy Russia's capabilities. That's the last thing Putin wants to do unless he wants to see the world end.

Another scenario: let's say the West does nothing and Russia took over Ukraine. Would Putin stop? The Eastern block is terrified of a Russian invasion. They do not want to live under Putin's regime. Let's say Putin did not stop, and then eventually NATO will have to step in to defend. If Putin did stop, he would have difficulty suppressing insurgence with a weakened military.

So the whole war in Ukraine is a disaster for Putin and Russia: they didn't expect a strong Western response, their conventional military is weak (asking North Korea help nearly 3 years in shows weakness), they've become a pariah state that depends on China, and their economy could collapse in the next 5 to 10 years.

Question then: If Putin is so concerned about Russia's security against NATO and that he wouldn't invade a non-NATO country, why did Sweden and Finland join NATO? Finland borders Russia giving easy access for NATO to invade. 

I know war sucks and I see why many people are pissed off with the US being indirectly involved, but don't fall for disinformation.

There are several angles to see this. First, Russia will likely escalate, either by trying to use more devastating tactics in Ukraine, or by arming the US' enemies, or both. Second, this could help Ukraine prevent Russian attacks on their infrastructure by destroying the weapons used against them inside Russia. Third, this could also help Ukraine by disrupting Russia's logistics and manufacturing, which could restrict Russia's mobilization of troops and equipment. Fourth, if the damage in Russia is severe, Russia may be tempted to use tactical nuclear weapons in Ukraine. Overall, this will help Ukraine, but it won't help them win the war because they just can't. Ukraine has a demographic disadvantage, disparity that will become even more pronounced as the war continues. Second, damage to Ukraine's infrastructure will continue to accumulate overtime, making it harder to rebuild after the end of the war. Third, Ukraine does not have nuclear weapons. If Russia sees itself in danger, they will use tactical nuclear weapons in Ukraine. In conclusion, this was a war that Ukraine could not fully win from the beginning given US and NATO doctrine, which is to avoid direct confrontation with Russia. Getting rid of Putin would not help, as Russia sees Ukraine as an existential issue, so it wouldn't matter who was in charge. This war needed to be prevented before it became a war. Realistically speaking, Ukraine will effectively lose part of their territory, and my prediction is that Russia will not sign a peace treaty, as doing so would allow what is left of Ukraine from joining NATO. That is not in Russia's interest; Russia wants a buffer or control the land between them and the Carpathian Mountains. They will only sign a truce or armistice, which would prevent Ukraine from joining NATO, as they would still be technically at war with Russia. If the US and Europe wanted to prevent this outcome once it became clear that Russia was about to invade Ukraine in 2022, they should have mobilized large amounts of troops on Russia's borders and forced Russia to similarly move their troops to keep them away from Ukraine and to bankrupt them (moving troops costs money). NATO and the US won't do this, so the outcome of this war was already decided before it began.

Self-neuralizing mines are not 100% reliable. They can still be dangerous even when rendered "inert" by time (the battery that sets off the explosive running out). It becomes far less likely they'll explode but some of them still can because the explosive material and vessel are still there. It's like shooting an inert grenade. 99% of the time the grenade will just break and never explode, but rarely the detonator gets hit and it instantly explodes. In the case of electronically triggered landlines maybe a keyfob on the same frequency as the detonator unlocking a car nearby triggers it and it explodes or maybe it getting run over by a farm tractor causes a spark against the explosive material and some poor guy becomes a cripple.

RS-26 Rubezh is a ballistic missile of medium range, which is normally designed to carry nuclear warhead. It was developed by the Moscow Institute of Thermal Engineering as part of the Avangard program. It was created on the basis of the RS-24 Yars. Information about this mobile missile system, like its rocket, is completely classified.

The RS-26 reportedly has a starting weight of about 40-50 tons and is capable of delivering 4 separate combat units at a distance of 2,000 to 6,000 kilometers. Its warhead is three times larger than the Iskander‚Äôs warhead. Accordingly, it is much more powerful.

It has an advanced protection against the missile defense system and reportedly four individual thermonuclear warheads with a capacity of 150-300 kilotons each. No foreign air defense system is reportedly able to intercept it.

The Rubezh missile is aimed at carrying out nuclear strikes but in apparently in today‚Äôs attack the combat units were equipped with metal blanks. The published footage drone Dnipro shows the kinetic effect of the use of such ammunition. It is possible that the rocket was equipped with a Avangard-R hypersonic glider.


The footage also shows that the launched rocket had 6 combat units with 6 warheads in each. It is possible that the Russian military used its secret RS-27 or Yars missiles of the same type.

After today‚Äôs strikes, the world will not be the same. Showing its advanced missile systems in action, Russia has demonstrated that it possesses unique missile technologies and is ready to use them effectively. In the event of the transformation of the conflict in Ukraine into a full-scale war with NATO, such complexes can already be used with standard nuclear ammunition.

The exact number of missiles of this type in service with the Russian military is secret. According to open sources, the Russian Federation possesses at least 200 RS-26 Rubezh and PC-24 Yars missiles, which is more than enough to deal series of devastating blows on its enemies.

Russia responded to escalation. Now the ball is in Western court. The further steps are yet to come but it is clear that the provocations, including strikes with Western cruise missiles on Russian critical military, transport and energy infrastructure will be paid at too high price.

The flight time to the target located about 800 kilometers away is estimated to be less than 5 minutes. The speed of the combat units at the final stage of the flight was about 5-7 kilometers per second.

The RS-26 Rubezh is a ballistic missile of medium range, which is normally designed to carry nuclear warhead. It was developed by the Moscow Institute of Thermal Engineering as part of the Avangard program. It was created on the basis of the RS-24 Yars. Information about this mobile missile system, like its rocket, is completely classified.

The RS-26 reportedly has a starting weight of about 40-50 tons and is capable of delivering 4 separate combat units at a distance of 2,000 to 6,000 kilometers. Its warhead is three times larger than the Iskander‚Äôs warhead. Accordingly, it is much more powerful.

It has an advanced protection against the missile defense system and reportedly four individual thermonuclear warheads with a capacity of 150-300 kilotons each. No foreign air defense system is reportedly able to intercept it.

The Rubezh missile is aimed at carrying out nuclear strikes but in apparently in today‚Äôs attack the combat units were equipped with metal blanks. The published footage drone Dnipro shows the kinetic effect of the use of such ammunition. It is possible that the rocket was equipped with a Avangard-R hypersonic glider.


The footage also shows that the launched rocket had 6 combat units with 6 warheads in each. It is possible that the Russian military used its secret RS-27 or Yars missiles of the same type.

After today‚Äôs strikes, the world will not be the same. Showing its advanced missile systems in action, Russia has demonstrated that it possesses unique missile technologies and is ready to use them effectively. In the event of the transformation of the conflict in Ukraine into a full-scale war with NATO, such complexes can already be used with standard nuclear ammunition.

The exact number of missiles of this type in service with the Russian military is secret. According to open sources, the Russian Federation possesses at least 200 RS-26 Rubezh and PC-24 Yars missiles, which is more than enough to deal series of devastating blows on its enemies.

Russia responded to escalation. Now the ball is in Western court. The further steps are yet to come but it is clear that the provocations, including strikes with Western cruise missiles on Russian critical military, transport and energy infrastructure will be paid at too high price.
